## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, where stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic constitutive laws and on temperature through thermal softening of elastic modulus and yield strength.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T) (elastic modulus linearly decreasing with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain for plastic deformation)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with hardening)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Voce hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon)) * (1 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with linear softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(-c1 * T) (Arrhenius-type thermal activation)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic response)
- Ludwik equation with temperature: sigma = c0 * T**c1 * epsilon**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Hyperbolic tangent hardening: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (1 - c2 * T) (saturating stress with thermal softening)
- Swift law: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (hardening with pre-strain offset)
- Thermal activation flow: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (thermally activated plastic flow)
- Bilinear model: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon * T (strain-temperature cross coupling)
- Hollomon with melting: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - (c2 * T)**c3) (power hardening with homologous temperature softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (1 - (c*T)**n) applied to stress
- Strain hardening saturation → exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)) or tanh-based forms
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with 0 < n < 1 for work-hardening materials
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → exp(-c/T) or exp(-c*T) multiplicative factors for thermally activated processes
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → additive decomposition: linear term in epsilon plus nonlinear hardening term
- Homologous temperature scaling → T appears as (T/T_melt) raised to a power, controlling softening rate
- Strain-temperature coupling → product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 indicating coupled thermo-mechanical response
- Pre-strain or yield offset → (epsilon + c)**n rather than epsilon**n to model initial yield behavior
